:Problem 4. Point O is the center of the circumcircle of triangle ABC with sides BC=8 and AC=4. Find the length of side AB if the length of the vector 4 overrightarrow{OA} - overrightarrow{OB} - 3 overrightarrow{OC} is 10.

:Answer: 5.Answer: Let the radius of the circumscribed circle be denoted by R. Then for any numbers x, y, z, the following equality holds:begin{aligned}& (x overrightarrow{O A}+y overrightarrow{O B}+z overrightarrow{O C})^{2}= & =x^{2} O A^{2}+y^{2} O B^{2}+z^{2} O C^{2}+2 x y(overrightarrow{O A} cdot overrightarrow{O B})+2 y z(overrightarrow{O B} cdot overrightarrow{O C})+2 x z(overrightarrow{O A} cdot overrightarrow{O C})= & =left(x^{2}+y^{2}+z^{2}right) R^{2}+x yleft(O A^{2}+O B^{2}-A B^{2}right)+y zleft(O B^{2}+O C^{2}-B C^{2}right)+x zleft(O A^{2}+O C^{2}-A C^{2}right)= & =left(x^{2}+y^{2}+z^{2}+2 x y+2 y z+2 x zright) R^{2}-x y A B^{2}-y z B C^{2}-x z A C^{2}= & =(x+y+z)^{2} R^{2}-x y A B^{2}-y z B C^{2}-x z A C^{2}end{aligned}Then, for x=4, y=-1, z=-3, we obtain the equality 10^{2}=0 cdot R^{2}+4 A B^{2}-3 B C^{2}+12 A C^{2}, from which A B^{2}=frac{1}{4}left(100-12 A C^{2}+3 B C^{2}right)=25, i.e., A B=5.

Finding ( m ) and ( n ): - The line ( x + y - 2 = 0 ) has a slope of -1. Therefore, the derivative of ( f(x) ) at ( x = 1 ) must be -1. - Given ( f(1) = -2 ), substituting ( x = 1 ) into ( f(x) ) gives ( n = -2 ). - The derivative ( f'(x) = frac{m}{x} + n ). At ( x = 1 ), ( f'(1) = m + n = -1 ). Substituting ( n = -2 ), we get ( m - 2 = -1 ), hence ( m = 1 ).2. Monotonicity Intervals: - The derivative ( f'(x) = frac{1}{x} - 2 ). - Setting ( f'(x) = 0 ) gives ( frac{1}{x} - 2 = 0 Rightarrow x = frac{1}{2} ). - For ( 0 < x < frac{1}{2} ), ( f'(x) > 0 ), so ( f(x) ) is increasing. - For ( x > frac{1}{2} ), ( f'(x) < 0 ), so ( f(x) ) is decreasing. Finding the Maximum ( t ): - The function ( h(x) = frac{-x^2 + 2x}{ln{x} - x} ) is increasing on ( [2, e] ). - Evaluating ( h(x) ) at ( x = e ) gives ( frac{-e^2 + 2e}{1 - e} = frac{e(e - 2)}{e - 1} ). The maximum value of ( t ) is ( boxed{dfrac{e(e - 2)}{e - 1}} ).]

:()Differentiating f(x) we get f'(x) = frac{m}{x} + n. Since the tangent of f(x) at point (1, f(1)) is parallel to the line x + y - 2 = 0, it follows that f'(1) = m + n = -1. Also, given that f(1) = n = -2, we find m = 1. Therefore, m = 1 and n = -2, and the function becomes f(x) = ln{x} - 2x, with the domain (0, +infty). Deriving f(x) again, we find f'(x) = frac{1}{x} - 2 = frac{1 - 2x}{x}. f'(x) > 0 implies 0 2 geq ln{x}, and therefore h'(x) geq 0 implying that h(x) is monotonically increasing on [1, e]. Hence, h_{text{max}}(x) = h(e) = frac{e(e - 2)}{ e - 1}, from which we conclude 0 < t leq frac{e(e - 2)}{e - 1}, and thus, the maximum value for the real number t is boxed{frac{e(e - 2)}{e - 1}}.

Understanding the Sum Calculation: - For each house, the contribution to the sum is the number of houses strictly lower than it. - To maximize this sum, we need to strategically arrange the heights of the houses.2. Key Insight: - Having many houses at lower floors allows taller houses to see more houses, thus contributing more to the sum. - This leads us to consider configurations with multiple houses at lower heights and fewer houses at higher heights.3. Two-Layer Configuration: - We consider houses with two distinct heights: 1-story and 2-story. - Let ( m ) be the number of 1-story houses and ( n ) be the number of 2-story houses. - The total number of floors is given by ( m + 2n = 30 ). - The sum ( S ) is calculated as ( S = m cdot n ).4. Maximizing the Product ( m cdot n ): - Solving ( m + 2n = 30 ) for ( m ) gives ( m = 30 - 2n ). - The product ( S = n(30 - 2n) ) is maximized when ( n = 7.5 ), but since ( n ) must be an integer, we check ( n = 7 ) and ( n = 8 ).5. Valid Configurations: - For ( n = 7 ): ( m = 30 - 2 cdot 7 = 16 ). Total houses: ( 16 + 7 = 23 ). - For ( n = 8 ): ( m = 30 - 2 cdot 8 = 14 ). Total houses: ( 14 + 8 = 22 ).6. Conclusion: - Both configurations yield the maximum sum ( S = 112 ). - The heights of the houses are 1-story and 2-story, with the respective counts. :Solution: 1) We will show that the project does not involve building houses with more than two floors. Assume the opposite, that such houses are planned. Take the lowest of them and reduce it by one floor, building an additional one-story house as a result. The sum of the numbers in question will decrease by the number of new two-story houses (and only in the case where we reduced a three-story house) and increase by the number of new houses with 2 or more floors (due to the built one-story house). Therefore, the sum of the new project is greater. Contradiction. Thus, Parallelnikov proposes to build only one- and two-story houses.2) Let the project involve building x one-story houses and y two-story houses. Then x+2y=30, and the sum will be equal to the product xy. We need to maximize the expression y(30-2y) on the interval [0; 15]. The maximum is achieved at the vertex of the parabola, at the point y=7.5. Considering that y is an integer, we get that the maximum value is achieved at y=7 or y=8 and is equal to 112. Accordingly, x is either 16 or 14.Answer: The sum is 112. Therefore, total squares is 1 + (m - 1) + (n - 1) - (gcd(m, n) - 1) = m + n - gcd(m, n). Which matches the formula. So that makes sense. So in this case, with m=1983 and n=999, the answer is 1983 + 999 - 3 = 2979. Therefore, the diagonal passes through 2979 fields. I think that's solid. Maybe I should check another example. Let's take 4x6 grid. gcd(4,6)=2. So 4 + 6 - 2 = 8. Let's see: the diagonal starts at (0,0), goes to (4,6). How many squares does it pass through? Let's imagine. It crosses vertical lines at x=1,2,3 and horizontal lines at y=1,2,3,4,5. But overlaps occur at (2,3), since 2/4 = 3/6 1/2. So that's one overlap. Therefore, number of crossings is (4-1)+(6-1) - (2-1) = 3 +5 -1=7. Then total squares is 1 +7=8. Which matches. So formula works. Hence, applying to the original problem, 1983 +999 -3=2979. That's the answer.</think>The diagonal of an ( m times n ) chessboard passes through ( m + n - gcd(m, n) ) fields. For a ( 1983 times 999 ) chessboard:1. Compute ( gcd(1983, 999) ): - ( 1983 div 999 = 1 ) with remainder ( 984 ) - ( 999 div 984 = 1 ) with remainder ( 15 ) - ( 984 div 15 = 65 ) with remainder ( 9 ) - ( 15 div 9 = 1 ) with remainder ( 6 ) - ( 9 div 6 = 1 ) with remainder ( 3 ) - ( 6 div 3 = 2 ) with remainder ( 0 ) - Thus, ( gcd(1983, 999) = 3 )2. Apply the formula: [ 1983 + 999 - 3 = 2979 ]The diagonal passes through (boxed{2979}) fields.]

:Every field that the diagonal crosses cuts a segment from the diagonal. The two endpoints of such a segment are the intersection points of the diagonal and the perimeter of the field. Therefore, we need to count how many segments the intersection points formed by the boundary lines of the fields divide the diagonal into.The number of vertical lines is 1984, which means 1984 intersection points. The 1000 horizontal lines intersect the diagonal at 1000 points, but among these points, there will be some - for example, the first or the last - where vertical lines also pass. These points - that is, the vertices where the diagonal passes through - have been counted twice.If the diagonal passes through a vertex, then the resulting rectangle is similar to the original, and if the side of the field is a unit, then its sides are also integers.![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_05_02_7165c7f6665720eb24eag-1.jpg?height=501&width=892&top_left_y=568&top_left_x=603)For the sides, it holds thatfrac{a}{b}=frac{1983}{999} quad text { and } quad 1 leq a leq 1983Conversely, for every pair of integers (a, b) that satisfy (1), there is a rectangle, as shown in the diagram, or a vertex through which the diagonal of the chessboard passes.Since the greatest common divisor of 1983 and 999 is 3, from (1) we have (frac{a}{b}=frac{661}{333}), and this form cannot be simplified further. This means that (a) is an integer multiple of 661, and (b) is an integer multiple of 333. Moreover, (a leq 1983), so (1) has exactly 3 solutions, namelya=661, b=333 ; quad a=1322, b=666 quad a=1983, b=999Thus, the diagonal passes through four vertices in total, two of which are also vertices of the chessboard, and the other two are the trisection points of the diagonal.Therefore, the boundary lines of the fields intersect the diagonal line at (1984 + 1000 - 4 = 2980) points. The number of segments created is one less than this, so the diagonal of the chessboard passes through 2979 fields.Remarks. 1. In the solution, we also showed that if the sides of the chessboard are relatively prime, then the diagonal of the chessboard does not pass through any field vertex inside the board.2. It follows from the proof that the diagonal of a (k times n) chessboard passes through ((k+n+1)-d) fields, where (d) is the greatest common divisor of (k) and (n).
